## 16:04 EDT - Codex (Extractor Integrity Reviewer) - Value Board v4.9 round-11 NOT-CLEAR

- Scope/stability: Adversarially reviewed extractor `684d7a0a76ecb8738ac8e2fbd775bd1a39dd036f7200b3675d236843350b0223` and comp `1f5fa8107c8d5237ef5788f631a5a98a7a7a61d515f95af5ea1a23d4cfee9276`. Pre/post SHA-256 matched. The real history DB was read-only; mutations were confined to `/private/tmp/dg-r11-integrity.9pum3m`.
- Baseline reconciliation: `DG_AS_OF=2026-07-11 DG_AS_OF_REF=ed1a0ae680b2c5b698241c5a4151465c47391f42` exits 0 and reproduces 12,201 rows, cohort 468, board 340, disagreements 191, signals 145/149/46, David 24/27, movement 204 (133 rostered/71 FA), David 14/23 with five at 2+, and movers Jones/Legette/Bell/Gabriel/Bryant. Printed hashes match the ship note: Jul-09 `8996ade8bf337605`, Jul-11 `d2137f31f06a6840`; independently computed full digests are `8996ade8bf3376056dd0a132373898d2d7781214dac3107d14715172cebeeed7` and `d2137f31f06a6840840f5f5837cf6efbbbdc52974c75fb75d6e325fe7460a7c9`.
- P1 print-only integrity: The code computes a digest and prints only its first 16 hex characters; it contains no expected manifest, expected-hash input, comparison, or mismatch abort (`comp-v33-extract.py:472-478`). Changing Legette's Jul-09 stored delta `0.244 -> 0.276` under a full ref pin exited 0, changed Jul-09 hash `8996... -> ff2c494975955724`, and changed movement `204/14/5 -> 203/13/4`. Changing Jul-11 `0.276 -> 0.244` likewise exited 0 and changed only the Jul-11 digest (`d213... -> 531c78c5895699f8`). The digest is an externally comparable receipt, not enforced integrity.
- P1 date topology / endpoint completeness: The extractor takes the last two distinct date labels and asserts neither expected predecessor nor snapshot cardinality. Moving one Jul-09 row to a synthetic Jul-10 day made the full pin exit 0 on pair `Jul-10 (1 row) -> Jul-11 (12,201)`, reporting movement `1`, David `1/1`, and 23 newly comparable roster players. In live mode, deleting Jul-13 and retaining only one Jul-11 history row made the Jul-11 artifact date equal the latest history label; the new guard passed and the run exited 0 with a one-row latest endpoint. The guard correctly exits 1 for the ordinary stale-artifact case (Jul-11 artifact versus history through Jul-13), so it prevents date-label mixing but does not establish endpoint completeness.
- Hash-equality claim is not an `iff`: Semantically identical key-order/whitespace reserialization and reversed DB row order preserve both digests and outputs, as intended. But changing JSON numeric spelling `0.244 -> 0.2440` preserves Decimal value and every movement figure while changing the Jul-09 digest to `54ea9769f6f97cb3`, so matching hashes are not necessary for movement reproduction. Conversely, after removing the DB primary key, inserting an exact duplicate produced 12,202 physical Jul-09 rows but the dict comprehension silently collapsed them to 12,201, yielding the same digest/output; the real schema's composite primary key correctly rejects that insert. Prefix truncation also leaves only 64 bits. Equality is useful external evidence under the current schema/canonicalizer, not a mathematical or self-enforced equivalence.
- P2 labeling/schema boundary: Both hash lines call all 12,201 rows `renderable payloads`, while actual renderable counts are Jul-09 334, Jul-11 340, and Jul-13 336; the hash intentionally covers every row, but the count label is false. Invalid JSON fails nonzero with `JSONDecodeError`; valid `{}` for one prior-day player exits 0, changes its digest/population, and is accepted without payload-schema validation.
- Guard/current-live matrix: Ref-only exits 1; date/ref mismatch exits 1; unmodified refless Jul-11 exits 0 as `PINNED-DEGRADED` with baseline hashes/figures. Current live exits 0 on aligned Jul-13 artifact/history and reports Jul-11 `d2137f31f06a6840`, Jul-13 `f1827a4d0fa8b9d3`, movement 224, David 14/24, eight at 2+. The current Jul-13 full digest is `f1827a4d0fa8b9d3f229f00a6e028e395675fa5c17c7a5572b7982dc11171304`.
- Verification: `uvx ruff check docs/design-comps/comp-v33-extract.py` -> `All checks passed!`. No expected Jul-09/Jul-11 hash appears in the extractor or comp source; the values exist only in today's ledger ship note. ## 20:26 EDT - Codex (Retry Safety Reviewer) - Wake-ordering adversarial postflight

- Task result: **NOT CLEAR**. The draft's bounded-wait intent is directionally correct, but its current contract does not close overlap, restart, clock, provenance, or exact-boundary behavior. No spec, code, data, schedule, or `AGENT_SYNC.md` bytes were changed.
- **F1 - single-flight is required before a retry loop is safe.** The runner uses shared fixed `<target>.tmp` names (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:321-326`), takes per-invocation backups and may restore them after a later failure (`:569-590`), and upserts same-day history with last-write-wins conflict updates (`:381-422`). The existing rerun test proves a second payload replaces the first (`tests/contract/test_market_divergence_refresh_runner.py:539-574`). A 30-minute waiter widens the manual/duplicate-launch overlap window. The spec must require an OS-released exclusive process lock covering readiness polling through terminal marker/report/history, plus deterministic behavior for a non-owner. A stale `lockfile.exists()` protocol is insufficient after a crash.
- **F2 - `now` cannot remain frozen across retries.** The runner samples `now_fn()` once (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:472-473`), passes that frozen value into source freshness (`:530-539`), uses it for candidate provenance (`:543-553`), and records it as terminal `finished_at` (`:614-623`; degraded path `:475-484`). A naive loop therefore reports start time as finish time and compares every attempt to the invocation date even across UTC midnight. The contract needs a wall-clock sample per attempt/terminal event plus a monotonic deadline. It must define UTC normalization, backward/forward wall-clock jumps, and the exact deadline check independently of wall time.
- **F3 - retry count/window boundaries are undefined.** "Every 60s up to 30min" does not say whether the initial read counts, whether a final read occurs exactly at `t=1800`, or whether `retries_used` counts sleeps or reads. Pin one deterministic model (for example: read at `t=0`; at most 30 sleeps; final eligible read at `t=1800`; `retries_used=30` on exhaustion) and inject `sleep_fn` plus `monotonic_fn` for zero-wall-time REDs. The deadline check must occur before sleeping so oversleep cannot create an unbounded 31st interval.
- **F4 - freshness of the full dependency bundle is not specified.** Stage order resolves PVO once before the market read (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:460,503-541`). The PVO resolver accepts any hash-verified runtime marker and has no same-day constraint (`src/dynasty_genius/pvo_source.py:107-144`); the 09:30 PVO and 09:40 divergence jobs are both calendar-scheduled (`ops/launchd/com.davidleess.dynasty-model-pvo-refresh.plist:44-53`, `ops/launchd/com.davidleess.dynasty-market-divergence-refresh.plist:27-33`). After a wake, divergence can freeze yesterday's valid runtime, wait for today's FC, then publish a mixed-vintage result. The contract must either re-resolve and pin both verified dependencies when the gate opens, or explicitly state and justify that PVO same-day freshness is not part of this guard.
- **F5 - crash/restart is only process-bounded without persisted run identity/deadline.** A crash during the wait leaves the prior terminal marker in place because markers are terminal-only (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:475-498,612-646`), and a restart resets an in-memory retry budget. A crash after first pair replacement can also leave the already-acknowledged mixed pair because publication is per-file rather than cross-file atomic (`:569-590`). Define whether bounds are per process or per scheduled occurrence, what the health surface shows while waiting, and the restart behavior at wait, pair-publish, history, and marker boundaries. Do not claim exactly-once/idempotent output without a run identity/completion check; the current history guarantees no duplicate primary-key rows, not no duplicate or immutable writes.
- **F6 - downstream failure semantics need retry metadata and exactly-once placement.** Build, validation, publish, history, marker, and report must remain outside the market polling loop and execute at most once after a fresh snapshot is returned. `retries_used` must be carried through every later abort, including history failure after the pair is already fresh (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:598-610`), not only success/exhaustion. The current draft names only the marker; require marker/report agreement. Do not retry downstream failures under the source policy.
- **F7 - midnight semantics conflict with the producer boundary.** FC stamps `retrieved_at` and `snapshot_date` before fetch retries (`src/dynasty_genius/capture/fc_forward_capture_driver.py:146-162,174-205`). A capture begun before UTC midnight but committed after it remains prior-date. Because capture changes are explicitly out of scope, the spec must define freshness as producer-stamped capture-start date and accept this edge, or reopen the producer contract; the consumer loop alone cannot make completion-day semantics true.
- **F8 - completion-sentinel alternative is not in the declared scope.** A producer-owned handshake requires changing the capture writer, contrary to draft line 9. The existing capture report is plain `write_text`, not atomic (`src/dynasty_genius/capture/fc_forward_capture_driver.py:126-129`), so it is not an existing safe sentinel. Treat a handshake as a separate capture-side design, not an interchangeable implementation detail of this slice.
- **CLEAR - partial FC snapshot read:** the capture store validates before write and inserts raw/joinable rows in one SQLite transaction (`src/dynasty_genius/capture/fc_forward_capture_store.py:132-213`); the consumer reads latest/hash/rows through one connection (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:166-217`). A polling implementation that calls that whole reader on each attempt and carries its returned rows forward observes pre-commit or post-commit state, not a partially committed batch.
- **CLEAR - fresh-between-attempts / no poll-side writes:** if only `market_source_prior_date` is retryable, each attempt invokes the whole FC reader afresh, and the returned fresh payload is used directly, a source landing between attempts is picked up without a check/use reopen. Missing/empty/ambiguous/corrupt/unreadable sources should remain explicitly immediate failures unless the spec separately names them retryable. Polling must perform no build, tracked publish, or history write.
- Tests / checks: source and scheduler trace completed; focused current suites `tests/contract/test_market_divergence_refresh_runner.py` plus `tests/contract/test_phase0b_market_source_ownership_red.py` passed (`19 passed in 0.75s`). They contain no retry, deadline, overlap, restart, or crash-boundary coverage; that green result does not clear the draft.
- Files changed: `docs/agent-ledger/2026-07-13.md` only (bounded preflight and this postflight). The shared worktree was already dirty/untracked; unrelated changes were preserved.
- Handoff / next step: Require REDs for exact attempt/deadline counts, source fresh at each boundary, UTC rollover and wall-clock jumps, two concurrent invocations, crash/restart at every mutation boundary, PVO refresh during wait, and every downstream terminal failure preserving the final retry facts before this specification can reach technical CLEAR.

## 20:24 EDT - Codex wake-ordering marker/sentinel review postflight

- Task result: **NOT CLEAR**. Bounded polling of the committed FC PIT store is the lower-blast mechanism, but the draft does not yet specify marker-health transitions, a truthful terminal clock, or dependency re-resolution across the wait. No spec, code, data, schedule, or `AGENT_SYNC.md` bytes were changed.
- Marker-health finding: `market_divergence_capture` accepts only `status=ok`; the health evaluator applies status before freshness (`app/config/report_freshness.json:138-150`; `app/api/routes/system_health_models.py:418-487`). Retry attempts must leave the prior terminal marker untouched and log progress. A new `waiting` status would immediately become `producer_failed`; exhaustion should write the existing degraded reason, and success should replace it with `ok`.
- Terminal-clock finding: the runner samples `now` once at invocation start and reuses it for both degraded and successful `finished_at` (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:472-483,612-623`). A wait would backdate terminal health by up to 30 minutes. Re-sample the terminal wall clock after polling/build while using an independent monotonic deadline.
- Retry-metadata finding: `retries_used` is not exposed by the generic health reader/model (`app/api/routes/system_health_models.py:118-128,557-620`). It is valid only as forensic marker metadata unless API/config/OpenAPI scope is reopened. REDs should pin a nonnegative integer on immediate success, retry success, exhaustion, and later terminal aborts.
- Sentinel finding: the SQLite store is the authoritative completion boundary; full payload validation precedes one transaction for raw/joinable inserts (`src/dynasty_genius/capture/fc_forward_capture_store.py:132-213`). The existing FC report is not a safe completion sentinel: it is a plain non-atomic `write_text`, is stamped before fetch/retries, and is emitted after the DB commit with uncovered exception paths (`src/dynasty_genius/capture/fc_forward_capture_driver.py:126-129,146-226`). A real producer sentinel is a separate capture-side design and still cannot replace the consumer's committed-data check.
- PVO TOCTOU finding: the runner resolves and hash-verifies PVO before evaluating the market source, then reads the resolved fixed path only after that stage (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:503-555`; `src/dynasty_genius/pvo_source.py:107-144`). A 30-minute poll materially widens the verify/use gap. Re-resolve and pin/read the verified PVO pair only after the market gate opens, or reverify its hashes immediately before build.
- Atomicity finding: divergence marker replacement is atomic for one writer (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:321-326,425-426`), while the fixed `.tmp` name is not a process lock. Overlap/single-flight remains a separate required contract.
- Tests / checks: Focused current suites passed: `41 passed in 1.45s` across market-divergence health registration, refresh runner, and FC forward-capture contracts. The current tests do not clear the new wait/transition/TOCTOU semantics.
- Files changed: `docs/agent-ledger/2026-07-13.md` only (bounded preflight and this postflight); all review targets remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: Keep DB polling, add REDs for prior-marker health during wait, truthful terminal timestamps, terminal retry metadata, exhaustion recovery, and PVO replacement during wait; do not use the current FC report as a completion sentinel.

## 20:41 EDT - Codex wake-ordering clock/health subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v1.md` at SHA-256 `e3b1de5f2ed5f4338930c327d08b1396d7aa440da89d64c7d9c1d92778233d15`.
- Clock defect: C1 pins a local calendar date, but both production runners use UTC clocks and the FC producer stamps `snapshot_date` from UTC capture-start time (`scripts/run_fc_forward_capture.py:99-105`; `fc_forward_capture_driver.py:160-162`). The current consumer also maps every unequal date, including a future date, to retryable `market_source_prior_date` (`run_market_divergence_refresh.py:214-217`). The spec must choose UTC end to end, require aware clocks, distinguish source `< target` from source `> target`, and seed UTC/local rollover plus future-date fail-fast.
- PVO defect: post-gate resolution does not support the categorical C3 claim. The resolver hashes mutable paths and returns them (`pvo_source.py:128-143`); the consumer later reopens the path. A PVO producer can replace it between verification and consumption. Parse the exact bytes whose digest was checked (or pin an opened immutable fd), and validate the PVO marker's `source_as_of` against the target day; the resolver currently does no freshness check, so wake coalescing can still select yesterday's hash-valid marker while today's PVO build is running.
- Lock/marker defect: an `O_EXCL` lockfile is not crash-released, and a persisted monotonic timestamp is not comparable across reboot. Age-based deletion can also evict a live owner whose poll+downstream work exceeds the threshold. Use a kernel-released advisory lock held by fd or weaken/document the guarantee; crash/restart exactly-once still needs a durable run/phase contract rather than process locking alone.
- #148 defect: market divergence accepts only `status=ok` (`report_freshness.json:138-149`; contract fixture lines 26-45), not `ok/noop` as C5 states. Any main `skipped_concurrent` marker becomes `producer_failed` because status is evaluated first (`system_health_models.py:418-438`). It also violates C5's promise that the previous marker stays untouched while the lock owner waits. Only the lock owner may replace the registered marker; a non-owner should log/exit or write a separately named, non-health artifact. The spec also needs marker/report agreement and a single terminal-write ordering for report-write failure.
- RED completeness defect: line 33 omits the above boundaries plus immediate-fresh, exact-deadline/oversleep, invalid config, future source, backward/forward wall jumps, PVO replacement between resolve/load, stale-but-valid PVO marker, non-owner health state, crash/restart at publish/history, and every pre-/post-gate failure preserving `retries_used` without a second terminal marker.
- Mechanism check: bounded polling of the committed SQLite store is still the correct consumer-only v1 mechanism. Validation and raw/joinable writes share one transaction (`fc_forward_capture_store.py:132-213`); the existing report is written only after commit and is not an atomic readiness sentinel (`fc_forward_capture_driver.py:214-226`). A new producer sentinel remains a separate capture-side design.
- Tests / checks: Focused current suites passed: `44 passed in 1.51s` across runner, hardening, market-divergence capture-health registration, and FC capture-driver tests. They do not exercise the proposed wait, lock, rollover, or marker transitions.
- Files changed: This ledger only. Spec, code, tests, schedules, data, markers, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: Root reviewer should return the concrete v1 findings above; implementation and schedule remain David-gated.

## 20:43 EDT - Codex (Wake v1 state/lock reviewer) postflight

- Task result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v1.md` at SHA-256 `e3b1de5f2ed5f4338930c327d08b1396d7aa440da89d64c7d9c1d92778233d15`.
- Finding 1 (lock safety): spec line 21 calls an `O_EXCL` lockfile "crash-released", but such a file survives process death. Its age-only `>2xWINDOW` recovery can also steal from a live owner whose unbounded post-gate build/publication exceeds 60 minutes, while a persisted monotonic value is not a valid cross-reboot age. Use a kernel-released nonblocking advisory lock held by an open descriptor, or specify an owner-liveness/start-identity protocol that never removes a live lock; age alone is insufficient.
- Finding 2 (non-owner write collision): line 22 makes the losing invocation write `skipped_concurrent` while line 26 promises the previous terminal marker remains untouched during the owner's wait. If this is the canonical #148 marker, it creates a second writer, overwrites truthful health, and evaluates as producer failure because `market_divergence.success_status` is only `ok` (`app/config/report_freshness.json:138-149`). Require no canonical marker write by a non-owner; use structured stdout or a separate per-invocation audit artifact if needed.
- Finding 3 (exactly-once/restart overclaim): line 23's lock and loop placement provide at most one owner and one call per invocation, not exactly-once effects across a crash. The current durable sequence is two non-cross-file-atomic replacements, then a separate SQLite upsert, then marker/report (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:569-644`). Crashes can leave latest-only, pair-without-history, or data-without-terminal-marker states; a restart repeats writes, and same-day history is last-write-wins (`:381-422`). Define those recovery states and either add durable run/phase identity or weaken the claim to per-invocation at-most-once plus tested idempotent reconciliation.
- Finding 4 (retry comparison domain): lines 6-8 pin a local target date even though the FC producer stamps `snapshot_date` from a UTC clock (`scripts/run_fc_forward_capture.py:99-105`; `fc_forward_capture_driver.py:160-162`). The current reader also maps every date inequality, including a future-dated source, to `market_source_prior_date` (`run_market_divergence_refresh.py:214-217`). Pin the target in the producer's UTC date domain and make only `source_date < target` retryable; `source_date > target` must fail immediately.
- Finding 5 (deadline/config boundary): lines 9-10 do not define validation for configurable WINDOW/INTERVAL or a clipped final sleep. Zero/non-finite interval can busy-loop; negative/non-finite window is incoherent; ordinary read time or scheduler oversleep moves the purported "AT deadline" read past the bound. Require finite positive values, define `sleep(min(INTERVAL, remaining))`, and define whether the one post-sleep deadline observation is eligible when it occurs late. Seed initial-fresh, exact boundary, interval>window, zero/negative/non-finite config, and stale-to-fatal transitions.
- Finding 6 (terminal metadata/status): line 27 says `ok`/`noop` are accepted, but the market-divergence registration accepts only `ok`. It also requires `retries_used` only on the marker, leaving the report able to disagree. Pin `status=ok` as the sole healthy terminal value and require the same nonnegative retry count in marker and report for immediate failure, success, exhaustion, and every later failure.
- Finding 7 (verification inadequacy): line 33 lacks restart-at-each-durable-boundary, owner crash/release, live-owner-not-stolen, non-owner-no-canonical-write, future source, exact deadline/invalid config, and marker/report agreement seeds. Those are required before the proposed contracts can be falsified.
- Checks performed: line-by-line state trace for immediate fresh, stale/fresh, deadline/oversleep, UTC/local rollover, future source, concurrent owner/non-owner, owner crash, and restart after each durable boundary; current runner publication/history and #148 registration traced directly; repository search confirms no current REDs for retries, locks, cross-midnight, or `retries_used`.
- Files changed: today's ledger only. Spec, code, tests, data, schedules, markers, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only; no live jobs ran.
- Product alignment: preserves honest daily freshness without replacing a wake race with unsafe lock stealing, false health, or unearned exactly-once claims.
- Handoff / next step: Revise C1/C4/C5 and expand the RED matrix; fresh bytes require a new adversarial pass before spec CLEAR.

## 20:56 EDT - Codex wake-ordering v2 clock/PVO subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v2.md` at verified SHA-256 `79ba9a1afd46c32442fbac73677732d20cd21c3600a557b07f5d56b695f0ca5f`.
- Timing-contract defect: v2 calls the state machine UTC-exact but drops v1's actual `WINDOW=30min` / `INTERVAL=60s` defaults and states neither units nor configuration source. Lines 13-15 therefore cannot determine the number/timing of polling reads or reproduce the observed mechanism. Pin governed defaults and units plus the override surface; validate exact `int` values (reject bool/wrong type), and seed the defaults as well as invalid overrides.
- Deadline-order defect: line 14 says to re-check the deadline before reading, then separately promises a final read at deadline expiry. Those branches conflict when the clipped sleep returns at or beyond the deadline. Pin executable order: sleep clipped remaining time, sample monotonic, execute exactly one final full read even at/after expiry, sample UTC after that read, apply rollover, classify, then exhaust only if still prior-date. State whether a large overshoot may accept data that arrived after the nominal window.
- PVO-vintage defect: `ResolvedPvoSource.source_as_of` is optional/opaque (`src/dynasty_genius/pvo_source.py:47,141`), while line 23 says only that it "must fall" on the target UTC day. Require a non-null, parseable timezone-aware timestamp, normalize it to UTC before comparing dates, and bind it from the same ready-marker snapshot whose two artifact digests are verified against the exact in-memory bytes. Reject missing, malformed, naive, and offset-crossing dates; do not compare the timestamp's lexical/local date.
- RED-matrix defect: lines 37-38 omit the C2 cross-midnight path entirely, despite v1 review explicitly requiring it. They also omit immediate-fresh/zero-retry, wall-clock jump, stale-to-fatal transition, malformed/missing/naive/offset-crossing `source_as_of`, and bool/wrong-type/non-finite timing config. These are necessary to falsify the new contracts rather than merely restate them.
- Checks performed: exact SHA and v1-to-v2 diff; line-by-line simulations of immediate fresh, stale/fresh, interval=window, clipped deadline, overshoot, and UTC rollover; source trace of FC UTC capture-start stamping (`fc_forward_capture_driver.py:160-162`), PVO ready-marker timestamp production (`scripts/run_pvo_refresh.py:371-382`), and resolver optional/opaque metadata plus hash-by-path behavior (`pvo_source.py:38-49,128-143`). No implementation tests were rerun in this bounded lane; root review owns the shared focused-suite result.
- Files changed: this ledger append only. Spec, code, tests, configs, schedules, data, markers, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: Root reviewer should carry these bounded timing/PVO/RED findings into the v2 verdict; implementation and schedule remain David-gated.

## 20:57 EDT - Codex wake-ordering v2 restart/publication subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v2.md` at verified SHA-256 `79ba9a1afd46c32442fbac73677732d20cd21c3600a557b07f5d56b695f0ca5f`.
- Pair-publication defect: C4 lines 29-30 calls the tracked pair an atomic/idempotent restart boundary, but the current contract explicitly publishes latest then coverage with only per-file atomicity (`scripts/run_market_divergence_refresh.py:13-18,329-340,569-590`). A process death after the first replace leaves mixed generations while C5 preserves the previous `status=ok` marker. A later run that aborts before publication leaves the mix intact; one that snapshots the mix and then fails can restore it. Require a true pair commit/reconciliation protocol or narrow the claim and force health/consumers degraded until both generation-linked files are verified; seed process death after each rename and both failing/successful restarts.
- Terminal-output defect: C5 lines 33-35 requires one terminal write plus marker/report agreement, but marker and report are independent file replacements and their ordering/failure contract is absent (`run_market_divergence_refresh.py:425-434,612-644`). Marker-first success can expose false `ok`; report-first can expose an optimistic report beside an old marker; a persistent write failure makes unconditional agreement impossible. Name the marker as canonical health truth, specify success/failure ordering and fallback semantics, and qualify agreement to cases where both terminal writes succeed, or introduce one durable terminal envelope. Seed exception/process death immediately before and after each write.
- Lock-acquisition defect: C4 lines 27-28 neither requires nonblocking acquisition nor selects one locking primitive/path. A blocking exclusive acquisition lets the supposed non-owner wait, later acquire, and perform a second canonical refresh; `flock` and `lockf` should not be left interchangeable. Pin one fixed lock path and primitive, `LOCK_EX|LOCK_NB`, contention-only exit 0, other acquisition failures as terminal, acquisition before canonical IO, and `finally` release; use a two-process RED.
- History-idempotence defect: C4 line 30 treats the per-day upsert as clean restart idempotence, but `_upsert_history` only inserts/updates (`run_market_divergence_refresh.py:381-422`) and never removes same-day rows absent from a changed rerun. Because PVO is deliberately re-resolved after the wait, a restart can produce a changed same-day set and leave stale union rows. Require exact-set reconciliation in one transaction, or narrow the guarantee to an identical candidate and prove all target-day inputs immutable. Seed first candidate `{A,B}` followed by `{A}`.
- Checks performed: verified declared spec SHA; line-by-line crash trace across lock acquisition, first/second pair replacement, history transaction, marker, and report; current runner helpers/publication/history/terminal sequence inspection; current partial-publish and same-set history tests inspected; consumer search confirmed the player API reads the latest artifact independently while other workflows retain the separate coverage path.
- Files changed: this ledger append only. Spec, source, tests, configs, schedules, data, runtime artifacts, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: Root reviewer should include these publication/restart findings in the v2 verdict. Implementation and schedule remain David-gated.

## 21:39 EDT - Codex wake-v5 loop/lock/schema subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for standalone `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v5.md` at verified SHA-256 `3365f417a7539b2762528eb9accf8a706b4b03ee7a7a6a59204906ec39176a5c`.
- Rollover defect: G1 now catches a market read that straddles UTC midnight, but there is no final UTC-date check after PVO byte verification/build and immediately before rename-1. A fresh market read at 23:59:59 can be followed by PVO/build crossing midnight and still publish target-day outputs on the next day. Add a prepublication rollover terminal and matrix row.
- Deadline-loop ambiguity: step 4 still expresses sleep from `deadline - now_mono` without saying it uses the post-read monotonic sample. A read that returns just before the deadline can therefore sleep using the older pre-read sample and push the final read materially past the bound. Name `post_read_mono`, compute remaining time from it, and seed a slow-but-pre-deadline read.
- Marker-schema contradiction: line 48 calls generation id and both output hashes required on the complete marker while line 50 applies the same contract to config/source/PVO failures that produced no outputs. Split schemas: `ok` requires valid generation/output hashes; `degraded` requires attempt metadata/reason but must not fabricate output hashes. Pin exact status vocabulary to `ok|degraded`, `reason` required iff degraded, and timezone-aware terminal UTC `finished_at` sampled at the marker attempt.
- Hash-contract residue: G2 computes three input hashes but no marker/report schema records them, leaving the input-digest work unobservable. Canonical market JSON also needs a single enclosing array, `allow_nan=False`, and a nonempty string `player_key` contract; row 32 covers only missing/duplicate keys, not wrong-type/blank/non-finite data.
- Matrix contradiction: row 16 is generic marker-write failure, while row 23 says the loader refuses every row-16 state. A marker failure on a pre-gate degraded attempt changes no pair, so the prior A marker/pair remains valid and the loader should continue serving A; only an after-output success-marker failure creates the mismatch. Split those states and expected health outcomes.
- Clear portions: `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX|LOCK_NB)` ownership, Darwin/Linux `EWOULDBLOCK`/`EAGAIN` contention classification, lock-before-canonical-I/O, no-lock canonical silence, post-read deadline designation, required output-hash recomputation, and missing/duplicate `player_key` fail-close are coherent.
- Checks: Verified declared SHA; diffed v4->v5; simulated immediate, slow-read, exact-deadline, overshoot, cross-midnight during market read, cross-midnight during PVO/build, config-with/without ownership, success/failure marker writes, and matrix rows 1-32. No implementation tests rerun in this bounded spec-only lane; no live producer ran.
- Files changed: Today's ledger only. Spec, source, tests, configs, schedules, data, runtime artifacts, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: Root reviewer should carry the five residual contract/matrix findings; implementation and schedule remain David-gated.

## 21:37 EDT - Codex wake-ordering v5 commit/history subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v5.md` at unchanged SHA-256 `3365f417a7539b2762528eb9accf8a706b4b03ee7a7a6a59204906ec39176a5c`.
- History-authority defect: G7 calls a post-transaction/pre-marker history generation detectable by comparing its day-content hash to the marker's committed run, but neither G7 nor the complete marker schema stores a history generation/hash/count. The marker binds only latest+coverage. The cited `DG_MOVEMENT_HASHES` mechanism is mandatory only for ref-pinned extractor runs (`comp-v33-extract.py:535-538`), not ordinary live/unpinned history readers. Persist a canonical per-day batch hash/generation in history metadata and define the reader contract, or remove the marker-comparison/detectability claim and state the live consequence honestly.
- Report-commit defect: the shared success report remains physically `provisional=true` forever because marker-last performs no second report write. The spec says a matching marker clears it but defines no report validation/read contract. Require every report reader to validate same-generation ok marker plus exact output hashes (or make the report generation-scoped and marker-referenced). Add the still-missing kill-after-report/pre-marker RED; marker-write exception is not equivalent to process death.
- Terminal-schema defect: G6 requires `generation_id` and both output hashes on every marker, including config/source/PVO failures that occur before a candidate generation exists, but does not define whether those fields describe the failed invocation, the standing pair, or are nullable. Pin separate attempted-vs-observed generation/hash semantics and matrix expectations for pre-publication failures.
- Matrix defect: row 27's `pinned evidence manifests unaffected` is misleading — a history mutation leaves the manifest bytes unchanged but makes the pinned read abort; live reads remain unprotected. Row 28's convergence claim is also unearned: a failed restart that reaches G7 can authoritatively replace the day again. The guaranteed property is atomic exact-set replacement per transaction, not convergence to a named generation.
- Explicit clears: G3 pair generation equality is coherent; G4 now mandates recomputation of both hashes from the exact returned bytes and fails on missing/malformed hashes; rows 25-26 correctly cover same-generation tampering and malformed marker hashes.
- Tests / checks: exact spec SHA verified before and after; line audit of G3/G4/G6/G7 and rows 25-30; current extractor manifest enforcement and current history/report write paths traced. No implementation tests rerun in this bounded spec-only lane; root review owns the shared focused-suite result.
- Files changed: this ledger append only. Spec, source, tests, configs, schedules, data, runtime artifacts, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.
- Handoff / next step: close the history metadata/read contract, report-validation contract, and pre-publication failure schema, then return fresh standalone bytes. Implementation and schedule remain David-gated.

## 21:43 EDT - Codex wake-ordering v5 repo-feasibility subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v5.md` at verified SHA-256 `3365f417a7539b2762528eb9accf8a706b4b03ee7a7a6a59204906ec39176a5c`.
- Enforcement-boundary defect: BF-2 names player/trade readers, but the repo also has a direct league-opportunity reader and a second canonical writer. `scripts/build_universe_market_divergence.py` calls the legacy writer, `src/dynasty_genius/universe_market_divergence.py` writes both latest files without the flock/generation/marker protocol, and `scripts/refresh_league_intelligence.py` invokes that builder. G4/G5 therefore remain bypassable unless the spec declares one canonical writer and redirects/retires every other writer, plus migrates every direct reader to the verified loader.
- Health-schema defect: G4 requires #148 to recompute both pair hashes and verify three generations, but current `ReportArtifactConfig` supplies only the marker path/field names, `ReportArtifactFact` has no generation/hash facts, and the reader opens only that one configured file. The spec must pin the companion artifact-path fields, exact marker/artifact field names, validation/failure bases, and config migration; otherwise matrix rows 14/15/23/25/26 are not executable against the shipped health abstraction.
- Terminal-schema defect: G6's complete marker requires `generation_id` and both output hashes, then applies the same schema to config/source/PVO failures that have no candidate outputs. Split strict ok/degraded schemas and pin exact names/types: canonical UUID4 and lowercase 64-hex `latest_sha256`/`coverage_sha256` for ok; nonempty `reason` and explicit omitted/null generation/hash semantics for degraded; timezone-aware UTC `finished_at`; strict non-bool nonnegative `retries_used`; `decision_supported=false`.
- History-detectability defect: G7 claims a history day-content hash can be compared to the marker's committed run, but neither the marker schema nor the current history table stores a history hash/generation/count. `DG_MOVEMENT_HASHES` is an external evidence manifest, not a live marker/history binding. Persist and validate canonical history metadata or narrow the claim to pair/marker mismatch plus manifest-gated evidence. Also pin the history row identity and fail closed on missing/duplicate IDs; the current writer skips missing IDs and upserts duplicates, which cannot prove the promised full exact set.
- Matrix gap: the table calls itself complete but omits the legacy-writer/reader bypasses, malformed JSON/root types, malformed/reused generation IDs, strict hash/timestamp/retry/reason/decision field validation, health-config companion-path failures, history missing/duplicate IDs and transaction rollback, and canonical market-row wrong-type/blank/non-finite inputs.

Existing focused suites were not rerun in this read-only subreview; no live producer ran.

Record the three input hashes and finish the canonical market domain (one enclosing array, `allow_nan=False`, nonempty string `player_key`, finite values); row 32 is too narrow.
- Explicit clears: bounded polling of the transactional FC SQLite store remains the correct mechanism; G3 three-way pair generation, mandatory exact-byte output-hash verification in G4, and G5 `flock` ownership/no-lock silence are coherent.

Existing suites do not exercise the proposed retry/generation/loader contracts.

## 22:00 EDT - Codex wake-v6 clock/hash/lock/terminal subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v6.md` at verified SHA-256 `ef9ee26c4dd678b1cb48637c68597ca0a7a4872e12f5dd900a24605faca366a7`.
- Terminal-report contradiction: G6's report schema requires generation id + both output hashes for every report, while write-ordering and pre-gate terminal rules require reports for config/source/PVO failures that produced no generation or output. Define strict ok/degraded report unions mirroring the marker (or scope line 58 explicitly to success and define the failure report shape); the current contract cannot produce a conforming pre-gate failure report.
- Health-union ordering gap: G4 says health always verifies companion generations/hashes, but a strict degraded marker deliberately carries null generation/hashes. Unless health status-gates first and performs pair verification ONLY for `status=ok`, a truthful degraded marker becomes `marker_hash_malformed` instead of #148 `producer_failed:<reason>`. Pin status-discriminated validation and seed it.
- Stale status/schema language: line 51 still permits `ok` plus unspecified failure statuses, contradicting line 54's exact `status in {ok,degraded}`. `finished_at` is required to be aware-UTC but not required to be freshly sampled at the terminal marker attempt, so the existing frozen-start-time bug remains conforming. Remove the stale vocabulary and pin terminal sampling.
- Matrix contradiction not actually split: prose line 57 says rows 16/23 split pre-gate from after-output marker failures, but row 16 remains generic and row 23 still requires refusal for every row-16 state. A pre-gate marker-attempt failure leaves A pair+ok marker valid and servable; an after-output failure leaves B/A mismatch and must refuse. Add two explicit rows.

Name each field and require lowercase 64-hex. The matrix has no digest-shape/tampering case and no strict terminal-union cases.

Add wrong-type/config-shape REDs. The post-read monotonic sleep basis and pre-rename UTC gate themselves are now coherent.
- Clear portions: G1 catches read-straddled deadline/date and build-time rollover; G2's enclosing-array encoding, `allow_nan=False`, stable nonempty `player_key`, and input-digest persistence are directionally sound; G5 `flock`, errno aliases, lock-before-canonical-I/O, and no-lock silence are coherent.

## 22:02 EDT - Codex wake-v6 enforcement/history/report subreview postflight

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v6.md` at verified SHA-256 `ef9ee26c4dd678b1cb48637c68597ca0a7a4872e12f5dd900a24605faca366a7`.
- G0 enforcement defect: the normative ownership claim covers pair, marker, report, and history, but rows 33-34 enforce only literal latest-file-basename hits. That cannot catch writes to the marker/report/history paths, dynamically assembled paths, or a new write through a shared helper. Pin the canonical mutation API/path registry and production-source allowlist, then test every canonical state object; basename grep alone cannot prove the claimed single writer/read path.
- #148 schema defect: G4 adds config fields and names three exact failure bases, but it does not define the corresponding strict `ReportArtifactFact` field or evaluator precedence that carries a companion verification failure into `ReportHealth.basis`. The current fact model has only status/reason and the evaluator can emit only malformed-status or `producer_failure:*`; overloading either cannot yield the three promised exact bases. Pin a verification-result fact field, status-first ordering (degraded marker reason wins; pair verification only for ok), and missing/unreadable/malformed companion outcomes.
- History-hash defect: `history_day_meta.content_sha256` has no canonical domain. G7 never pins row ordering, enclosing encoding, included columns, identity normalization, finite-value rules, or a single read transaction for metadata + rows. Writer and reader can therefore share the same accidental omission (for example hashing payload JSON while leaving `decision_supported` unauthenticated) and row 36 still passes. Pin the exact stored-row tuple/domain and snapshot read before claiming independent recomputation.
- History convergence/matrix defect: row 27's `pinned evidence manifests unaffected` is false in operational effect — same-day B replacement changes the day hash, so an unchanged A manifest makes the evidence reader abort. Line 66/row 28 also promise convergence on the next successful owning run, but a next-day owner writes a different capture date and never rewrites the failed day. Qualify this to a successful rerun for the same capture date and state that pinned evidence is invalid until its manifest is deliberately regenerated.
- Report-integrity defect: G6/G8 makes report commitment depend on matching its generation/output-hash strings to an ok marker, but the marker does not bind the report bytes and row 38 does not require the G4 exact-byte pair verification. A report can be mutated after commit while retaining those three fields and still be treated as committed; pair tampering can likewise pass the report-only check. Record/verify `report_sha256` on the marker (or strictly constrain report authority to marker fields) and require the report reader to traverse the verified pair loader.
- Additional reader-schema defect: G4 checks only marker status/generation/output hashes, not the complete strict ok shape promised by G6. A marker with `decision_supported=true`, bool/negative retries, a forbidden reason, malformed input digests, or extra fields could still authorize pair bytes. Require the centralized loader and health checker to use one strict discriminated marker validator and seed malformed-union cases.
- Checks: verified exact v6 bytes before and after; traced current alternate writers/direct readers, strict #148 config/fact/reader/evaluator, history writer and extractor, report writer, and matrix rows 33-38. No implementation tests or live producer ran in this read-only spec lane.
- Files changed: today's ledger append only. Spec, code, tests, configs, schedules, data, runtime artifacts, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.

The full refresh still runs 17.4 before 17.5 and restores upstream PVO artifacts on any later failure, so divergence/history/marker B can remain while PVO latest reverts to A; G4 still reports B healthy. If a pre-gate marker attempt fails, pair+marker A remain but report A has already been overwritten; A marker's `report_sha256` no longer matches. Row 16a is not fully servable. A first guarded run adds metadata only for its target day, so the prior day required for movement fails G7. The spec still contains generic failure-status language, incomplete report field sets, ambiguous null-vs-absent fields and untyped attempt metadata. - Report semantic-binding defect: hashing report bytes rejects later mutation but not an already inconsistent report. A committed reader must compare every duplicated generation/input/output/retry field against marker and hash+parse the same bytes.
- Clear portions: bounded polling; G1 post-read/deadline/prepublish UTC gates; G2 verified-byte PVO and canonical market-row digest; G5 `flock`; the explicit history→pair→report→marker order; status-first intent for valid degraded markers; report-byte hash against post-write mutation.

G7 requires one canonical enclosing array with byte-identical `payload_json`; the extractor instead concatenates unframed fields and hashes a parsed/re-serialized payload. Independent reproduction gave landed hashes `c2174d57...` / `2a58f382...`, but the specified raw-tuple algorithm gives `81853281...` / `721c0f91...`. A trailing-whitespace mutation and a duplicate-key mutation both left the landed Jul-09 digest unchanged, so an unchanged expected manifest can silently accept changed stored bytes (`spec:76-80`; `extractor:442-445,547-562`).
- The claimed strict JSON / No-Verdict evidence is not landed in the extractor. Its `json.loads(..., parse_float=Decimal)` accepts duplicate keys, NaN, Infinity, and `1e9999`; `json.dumps(..., default=str)` then hashes the lossy result. It reads verdict flags separately, outside one SQLite snapshot, defaults a missing flag to zero, accepts equality-equivalent falsey values, hardcodes `b"0"`, and never enforces recursive exact JSON `false` as required by the constitution (`extractor:438-445,551-561`; constitution `00:162`; spec `:76-78,136-143`). The spec's writer rule also says only truthy inputs fail, so `None`, `""`, and `0.0` remain silently coercible; exact input/output types and recursive sites need REDs.
- `guard_meta` is not durable against its named threat. A normal first-run create and a post-activation deleted-row/table state are indistinguishable from the information specified; the next owner can recreate a later `effective_from_date` and reclassify post-guard no-meta days as legacy. Pin an external/schema-migration activation state, ban automatic recreation after activation, define the singleton schema and atomic bootstrap order, and seed row/table deletion, date mutation, pre-guard DB restoration, and crash-around-bootstrap (`spec:79,141`).
- The history metadata union is internally incomplete: the pinned columns omit `legacy`, while the next paragraph requires it. No exact live-vs-legacy schema, `generation_id NULL iff legacy`, canonical date/hash/count/timestamp types, or prohibition on legacy backfill for days on/after `effective_from_date` is specified. Row 43 is therefore not executable enough to protect row 56 (`spec:75,79,128,135,141`).
- The active decision packet still pins the retired extractor SHA and old `8996ade8...` / `d2137f31...` hashes, and running its old full manifest against the current extractor aborts immediately. Frozen comp v4.13 embeds the same stale expected manifest in its builder note; do not reopen frozen pixels, but issue an external erratum/current reproduction record and version the old extractor semantics (`decision-packet:5-9`; `static-comp-v4.13.html:635`; spec `:77`).

- Input-basis verification defect: G2 records the PVO input digests, but G4 verifies only the divergence output pair and G6 only compares those input digests between marker/report. Nothing compares `input_pvo_sha256` / `input_pvo_coverage_sha256` with the currently resolved PVO bytes. Current `/players` and trade-market paths resolve/load PVO and divergence independently, so a normal later PVO generation C can be combined with a self-consistent divergence generation B while loader and #148 health remain green. The verified loader/health contract must reconcile the currently selected PVO pair to the marker input digests or the calling surface must fail closed as basis-mismatched; seed the ordinary next-PVO-publish window, not just rollback.
- Row-46 orchestration defect: banning restore does not establish `chain never mixes`. In the current stage order, 17.4 can commit divergence B and 17.5 can then fail, leaving `league_opportunity_latest` A. `league_pulse.py` independently loads posture/value/opportunity and its assembler accepts differing `captured_at` values, so B/B/A is still served. The spec needs a chain-level commit/generation barrier or explicit downstream partial-advance fail-close; alternatively narrow row 46 to the one invariant it actually proves. Current upstream stages also lack the claimed per-stage committed-generation mechanisms, so the universal migration is not executable from this standalone spec.
- Governed-reader scan defect: G0's history-db allowlist omits the standing offsite backup reader. `app/config/backup_manifest.json` names `app/data/market_divergence_history.db`, and `scripts/backup_irreplaceable_data.py` dynamically opens/snapshots manifest-listed SQLite stores. Because v8 explicitly excludes config path references from the scan, rows 33/34 can report zero unsanctioned readers while this governance-required reader exists. Add the backup workflow as a read-only exception with its exact access mode, and test dynamic/registry-driven access rather than basename literals alone.
- #148 confinement/schema defect: the proposed `companion_artifacts` / `output_hash_fields` contract still does not require exactly two unique, aligned entries, nonblank canonical repo-relative paths, resolve-time symlink confinement, or exact field literals. A duplicated latest path paired with duplicated `latest_sha256` can leave coverage unverified in a list-zip implementation. The generation-addressed marker `report_path` is likewise unconfined. Pin the exact canonical object table/regex, strict config validators, resolved-path boundary, and malformed-config outcome before calling the schema executable.
- G4 migration-semantics gap: row 34 proves only that direct reads disappeared. The four callers currently have materially different contracts (players required read, trade-market absent-to-empty degradation, opportunity builder hard failure, helper read); v8's “degraded/absent contract of the calling surface” leaves those outcomes undefined. Add caller-specific REDs so a generation/hash/basis mismatch cannot be silently translated into a genuine empty market lane.
- Tests / checks: exact SHA and v7->v8 diff; traced the full refresh order/restore path, current PVO and divergence readers, League Pulse multi-artifact assembly, #148 config/fact/evaluator code, and all production path literals; verified the dynamic backup-manifest reader; focused health/backup slice produced `62 passed, 1 failed` — the failure is the already-named 0-byte stray `app/data/valuation/market_divergence_history.db` omitted from the manifest, while the live 78 MB store is covered. No live producer ran.
- Files changed: today's ledger only. Spec, source, tests, configs, schedules, data, runtime artifacts, and `AGENT_SYNC.md` remained read-only.

- Result: **NOT CLEAR** for the bounded pointer/report/publication lane of `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-13-wake-ordering-guard-spec-v9.md` at verified SHA-256 `9448f5998591fc1a2795c7124c33562148d31809b872b0fcb15758eec989375f`.
- Dual-commit defect: G3 calls the pointer swap the pair's single atomic commit and the next line calls the ok marker the commit. After pointer A->B but before marker A->B, G4's required marker-pointer equality serves neither generation even though A's generation files remain. A caught pre-pointer publication error also writes a degraded marker and thereby blocks intact pointer-A. A direct state probe returned `loader_serves=false` for both states. Pin one atomic commit record, or explicitly specify a safe marker-generation fallback / separate latest-attempt health contract and accept/test any outage (`:36-42,56-61`).
- Pointer schema/ownership defect: the new canonical pointer has no strict schema (exact field names/types, UUID/path-generation agreement, decision flag, confined regular-file paths/no symlink, canonical basename) and no exact sibling-temp/atomic-write contract. G0's writer declaration and rows-33/34 scan inventory still list pair/marker/report/history but omit the pointer, so an alternate pointer writer/reader is not mechanically excluded (`:11,15,36,118-119`).
- Health-schema defect: #148 still configures fixed `companion_artifacts: [latest_path, coverage_path]`, but generation-addressed filenames are dynamic and discoverable only through the pointer. The executable health contract must configure and strictly validate the pointer, then open the two pointer-selected generation paths; the current exact-two static companion schema cannot implement G3 (`:36,42-44`).
- State-machine/stale-sweep defect: the normative order and matrix were not migrated. Active text still says publish gate before rename-1, rename-2 before marker, and `history -> rename-1 -> rename-2`; rows 14/15/23/27/40/47 model direct latest/coverage renames, row 46 still says `chain never mixes` despite line 13's disclosed `chain_mixed`, and row 17 retains forbidden `marker failed`. Row 59 is mislabeled: `new pair written, pointer old` is a crash BEFORE the swap; an atomic swap crash is old OR new, and the new-pointer/old-marker branch is missing (`:25,37,54-55,69-70,98-102,108,112,125,131-134,144`).
- GC/concurrent-reader defect: `keep last N` does not pin N, age/grace, cleanup phase, protected-set recheck, or a loader snapshot/retry protocol. A lock-free reader can snapshot pointer/marker A, then writer commits B and prunes A before it opens both A files; a direct temp probe reproduced `ENOENT` for both. Require an exact G5-owned GC algorithm plus reader fd/snapshot+bounded-retry semantics (or a grace/retention floor that covers active reads). Row 59's `orphans pruned later` otherwise has no normative basis (`:36,42,144`).
- Audit-only report residue: line 62 correctly says report failures bind report consumers only, but line 64 and rows 45/49 still say report disagreement refuses generic `commitment` and couple the pair loader into that read. Narrow them to report-consumer refusal while G4 pair service remains unaffected. The degraded marker shape also omits exact `report_path`/`report_sha256` semantics for a successfully-written attempt report versus `report_write_failed`, despite line 62 saying the marker references the report (`:59-65,130,134`).
- Temp/restart residue: row 48 says report/marker temps are `discarded`, but the contract only gives report stale-temp sweeping; it gives no marker- or pointer-temp sweep/ignore rule, and the row omits pointer-temp interruption entirely. Canonical files may remain untouched, but the claimed cleanup is not specified (`:57,62,133`).

- PVO cadence state-machine defect: v9 records only PVO input hashes on the divergence marker/report, not the input PVO `source_as_of`/source kind/generation. Hashes cannot establish NEWER versus OLDER, and the only matrix rows cover those two labels. Equal-vintage changed bytes, one-side PVO/coverage mismatch, unverified current PVO, seed fallback with no as-of, and identical bytes with a newer ready-marker stamp are undefined. The current resolver exposes `source_as_of` only from its separate ready marker and current callers then reopen the path after verification. Pin the provenance fields, exact-byte composite read, precedence, and REDs; a greater timestamp must also distinguish the bounded expected pre-divergence turnover from a multi-day stale comparison rather than treating every newer PVO as flat NORMAL (`spec :31-32,43,59,63,139-140`; `pvo_source.py:47,128-143`; `players.py:134-147`; `trade_market.py:72-90`).
- Trade market-basis defect: G2 records `input_market_rows_sha256`, but G4 reconciles only PVO. The trade endpoint separately fetches current FantasyCalc rows and then attaches a divergence context computed from the prior captured market rows; the response has one market timestamp and the divergence context carries no independent vintage. Normal next-market turnover can therefore present a current FC price beside an old model-minus-market delta. The trade composite contract must compare the current canonical market snapshot/hash to the divergence input or suppress/label only the divergence context until bases match (`spec :32,43-44`; `trade_market.py:269-293`; `market_reconciler.py:50-60,141-159,768-790`).
- Caller-contract defect: “players -> honest degraded/absent,” “trade endpoints -> refuse,” and “health -> named base” are not executable API outcomes. The player model has distinct market/divergence/degradation/caveat fields but no divergence-model-basis timestamp or `pvo_newer` state; trade refusal has no status/reason contract; the opportunity builder and generic reconciler named in the migration inventory have no mismatch behavior; and the matrix lacks caller-specific cases. Pin exact payload/status/caveat/HTTP behavior and require the opportunity producer to fail before publication rather than translate mismatch into an empty lane (`spec :14,43-44`; `players.py:95-125,293-310`; `build_league_opportunity_map.py:45-57`).
- Chain-lineage defect: line 13 is not a standalone contract. The refresh is a DAG, not `stage N -> stage N-1`: divergence branches from PVO+market, while opportunity consumes matrix+posture+divergence+roster-cut inputs. No stage-marker table/schema/path/commit mechanism, digest domain, DAG edge list, chain-health config, or surface behavior is pinned; current stage artifacts have no generation/input hashes and League Pulse independently assembles them. A #148 warning alone also does not disclose the mismatch on the user response. Row 46 still says `chain never mixes`, directly contradicting line 13's intended mixed-but-disclosed result. Pin the exact DAG and markers, include them in G0, and either carry `chain_mixed` plus all vintages on League Pulse or fail the surface (`spec :13,15,44,131`; `refresh_league_intelligence.py:23-34`; `build_league_opportunity_map.py:45-55`; `league_pulse.py:35-70`; `league_pulse_assembler.py:306-341`).
- #148 dependency/config defect: the proposed checked-in `companion_artifacts` are static while G3's pair paths are generation-addressed and selected by a pointer; moreover the config names neither the current verified PVO pair needed for `pvo_regressed` nor the stage markers needed for `chain_mixed`. Those advertised failure bases therefore cannot be derived from the declared schema. Configure a strict static pointer entry and logical slots, resolve and hash pointer-selected bytes, and pin separate PVO/chain dependency facts with exact status/basis precedence (`spec :36,42-44`; current `report_freshness.json:137-160`; `system_health_models.py:64-99,557-620`).
- G0 dynamic-scan defect: adding the backup workflow to an allowlist does not make the basename/path scan observe it. The required history path comes from `backup_manifest.json`, while `backup_irreplaceable_data.py` contains no history basename and opens the resolved source generically; the direct scan reproduced no hit for that script. The evidence extractor is also under `docs/`, explicitly outside scan scope despite being allowlisted. Choose and pin a real boundary/AST/registry test, including the exact required SQLite manifest entry and `mode=ro` source connection, rather than a vacuous literal grep (`spec :15,118-119,145`; `backup_manifest.json:5-7`; `backup_irreplaceable_data.py:181-218,363-369`).
